Shanghai's Honor to the Red Cross Ambulance Team

Due to the spread of war, the Chinese Red Cross Society had previously organized and dispatched an ambulance team for rescue operations. Now that the war has ended, the team has returned to Shanghai a few days ago. Yu Feipeng, Director-General of the Land, Sea, and Air Force Headquarters' Logistics, presented a large silver shield, and Liu Chuanlian, Director of the Logistics Hygiene Department, also presented a silver shield to Bao Kangning, the captain of the ambulance team. They were specially sent to Shanghai by Mr. Zhang Yunsen, along with a letter of appreciation. Director-General Yu's letter stated: "Dear Sirs, after Yan and Feng rebelled and caused chaos, the Central Government, in order to uphold its authority and rectify discipline, had no choice but to send troops to suppress them. Since the beginning of the war, it has lasted for half a year, and the casualties of soldiers have reached tens of thousands. We are grateful for your Society's enthusiasm and efforts to assist, providing treatment and healing, without distinction. Now that Qin and Long have been pacified and Hebei has been stabilized, we are promoting culture and restoring the country. Remembering your hard work, we are deeply impressed. We hereby present a silver shield for your safekeeping to express our gratitude. This is addressed to the General Office of the Chinese Red Cross Society." Director Liu's letter stated: "Dear Sirs, this year in May, Yan and Feng caused chaos, and the Central Government had no choice but to use force. The intensity of the battles on the Jinpu and Longhai lines was unprecedented. At that time, the layout of the hospitals had not yet been completed, and the wounded soldiers from the front line were sent down in large numbers, and it was difficult to delay their reception and treatment. We are grateful for your Society's firm support and the dispatch of Captain Bao to lead the team for rescue operations. Your medical skills saved the country, and your kindness was deeply appreciated by the Party and the country. Now that the stubborn enemies have been eliminated and the Party's foundation is firmly established, we are deeply moved by your hard work. In addition to the silver shield presented by our Director-General to thank all the colleagues of your Society for their achievements, we hereby present a small silver shield to Captain Bao to express our respect and admiration. We hope that your Society will continue to promote its great public welfare ideals. This is addressed to the General Office of the Chinese Red Cross Society." It is reported that the Red Cross stated that dispatching ambulance teams to treat wounded soldiers was their duty, and they dare not take credit for it. They have kept the shields as a souvenir and sent separate letters of thanks.

Petition for Disaster Relief in Huaiyin County

The Shanghai Chinese Jishang Society stated that Zhou Yuankai, the chairman of the Qingjiang Jishang Branch, and Wang Baohuai, the representative of the Huaiyin County Bandit Disaster Relief Committee, came to the meeting and stated that in Huaiyin County, where the National Army was stationed to suppress the rebellion this year, the garrison was weak, and bandits took the opportunity to plunder and burn. There were even cases where entire villages were left without a single house. They were in dire straits and requested relief. According to a joint letter from Han Zhao, Li Yushu, Liu Dingxin, Cao Bingqian, Ruan Kaiji and other executive committee members of the Huaiyin County Bandit Disaster Relief Committee, it said that there have always been many bandit problems in Jiangbei. Because the country has many problems and the suppressing troops are few, bandits are rising up like bees, and wherever they pass, it becomes a wasteland. They kidnap people and livestock, loot and burn houses. Compared to famine years, disaster victims still have livestock to sell, but now there are only empty barns; they used to have places to live, but now they are half scorched earth. In total, thousands of houses have been destroyed, and tens of thousands of people have been affected. They are exposed to the wind and sleep in the open, not only without clothes or food, but also without shelter. At this time when the north wind is howling and severe cold is approaching, they are suffering from both cold and hunger, and their lives are hopeless. Zhao and others could not bear to sit idly by, so they organized a relief committee. They deeply worry that the disaster is severe and the area is wide, and that a small amount of aid cannot save them. They can only rely on the generosity of kind people for relief grain and kind soup. They have always admired your Society's great compassion and desire to save all. The victims of the disaster urgently need help. They respectfully request your special assistance to save the lives of the people. The Society is currently handling winter relief and work relief projects in Shaanxi, Beiping, Liaoning, Zhoutai, Jiangsu and other places, and the funds used have already been considerable. They rely entirely on the voluntary donations of kind and charitable people. This year, due to the economic recession, donations have sharply declined. After listening to the statement of the Huaiyin County representative and the letter from the County Relief Association, the Society expressed its great sympathy. However, due to financial difficulties, they could not find a solution. They hope that many kind people in Suzhou will not ignore and fail to help them.

Verdict Announced in Case of Car Killing Vietnamese Police Officer

▲Driver Yu Xinkui's License Revoked ▲Compensation of 2,500 Yuan for Bereavement

In the French Concession, Vietnamese police officer No. 398 of the Songshan Road Police Station was on duty at the intersection of Pubo Road and Sapo Sai Road last month when he was hit and killed by two cars driven by drivers Sun Zulin and Yu Xinkui. The French Police Station summoned the two defendants to the French Public Court for investigation and concluded the case, with the verdict scheduled to be announced. Yesterday, on the date of the verdict announcement, the police station summoned the two parties. The Chinese and Western judges ordered each of the two defendants to pay a fine of 10 yuan and jointly compensate the family of the deceased with a bereavement payment of 2,500 yuan. Defendant Yu Xinkui had repeatedly violated regulations and his license was revoked and he was permanently prohibited from working as a driver, as a warning for the future.

Robbery and Injury Outside Dadongmen

Meng Defa, a 37-year-old man from Shaoxing, used to make a living as a boatman. He sailed a boat from his hometown to Shanghai a few days ago. At around 2 pm yesterday, he arrived at the Yongsheng Wharf in Nanshi. After anchoring, he carried 900 yuan to purchase goods on behalf of a customer and rushed ashore. He went straight to the Datong Salted Fish Shop at the Grand Wharf to order goods. He paid 100 yuan in advance on the spot, and kept the rest of the money in his waistband. Unexpectedly, when Meng took out the money from his pocket, two thugs happened to be standing on the side of the road and saw his pile of banknotes, and immediately had the idea of ​​coveting it. After Meng said goodbye and left, he planned to go to other places to shop, but the two thugs followed him. When he arrived near Longde Bridge outside Dadongmen, seeing that there were few people around, the two thugs jumped forward and carried out their robbery. Unexpectedly, Meng was very strong and the two were no match for him. Then one of the thugs took out a pistol, pulled the trigger, and fired a shot, hitting Defa's right arm. When ordinary pedestrians suddenly heard the gunshot, they gathered to watch. The thugs took the opportunity to escape, and the silver dollars were not taken. After receiving the news, the patrol officer of the responsible Public Security Bureau led the police to the scene, but the bandits had already fled. Later, Meng was accompanied by his friend Wang Jiren to the Shanghai Hospital. At 11:30 that evening, he was transferred to the Baolong Hospital, where the doctor tried to remove the bullet, applied medicine and treated him.

Free Talk

One Word of Wisdom

— Qiushui

▲Among animals, only humans blush. And only humans have a reason to blush.

▲To change a woman's mind is a difficult thing, unless you compromise with her.

▲Long-term borrowing inevitably leads to little hope of repayment. Protracted and difficult-to-resolve love affairs also often have no hope of success.

▲Women must have at least one touching thing. This is neither the brain nor the personality, but a loving attitude.

▲Men sometimes praise a beautiful woman and sometimes are moved by the heartstrings of a noble socialite. However, he must marry a loving wife.

▲A woman can simultaneously love two or more men for various different impulses and reasons. But men are like old-fashioned gramophones, capable of singing only one love song record. He has only one impulse and one reason for a woman.

▲Marriage is a major process in the lives of both men and women. In this process, men cease their childish affection for women and hope that women will treat them with a motherly attitude.

▲Divorce is a very effective surgical procedure in love. And divorce, like surgery, must leave a scar on that white flesh.

Record of an Unconventional Couple

— Wang Meiju

My friend, a descendant of a Jinshi from Zhongnan, possesses the handsomeness of Zifang and the talent of Zijian. His fiancée is a true descendant of Xie Daoyun, beautiful in appearance and intelligent within, not an ordinary woman. Last Sunday, I drove to visit them, but while the house was near, the person felt far away. On the table, pink envelopes piled up like layered peaks. Someone told me, "This gentleman is quite peculiar. The engaged couple troubles the Blue Bird with letters every day, conveying messages back and forth. There are even days when they receive three messages." I then jokingly wrote on the envelope, "The Blue Bird conveys sweet words all day long, when will the lovebirds be able to roost together?" Everyone who saw it laughed. One person even said, "Are you still unaware of the situation?"

A few days later, I visited again. We exchanged a smile upon meeting and arranged a banquet to catch up. I then asked, "Sir, you are so young and strong. Why delay the wedding and only send letters to communicate?" He replied, "My abilities are not yet sufficient to establish a household." However, this gentleman, although not born into wealth, has a fixed income and is famous in literary circles, his writings fetching high prices. His monthly income is quite substantial. His words must not be sincere, so I pressed him with wine, hoping he would reveal his true feelings after becoming drunk. His teacher, Mr. Gaoyang, who was present, said to me, "This is a naturally matched, unconventional couple. He once confided his sincerity to me." Zhongnan stopped the teacher with his eyes, but the teacher ignored him, speaking freely without reservation.

This gentleman values noble love and cherishes the union of spirits. The "Willow Catkin" also shares the same sentiment. Every ten days or so, she must visit Xutai to see his face. The letters they exchange are frequent and long, with both parties being of one mind. He says, "The love of an engaged couple is like fine wine, like sweet honey, like a flower about to bloom, like a moon about to be full. Once there is a physical union, although it may be delightful, it is the end. Nothing more can be added. Moreover, planning household affairs and raising children, even if love does not crack, mundane matters are enough to hinder pure love. It is better to remain neither close nor distant, like glue or lacquer, as it is today." After Gaoyang revealed his thoughts, Zhongnan also revealed a little under the influence of alcohol, saying, "I cherish this 'just right' time, learning from the 'celestial lovers' in the Daoist books, regarding each other as Yin and Yang." I laughed and said, "Then will it end here?" He said, "No. When it can no longer be delayed, we must also become a machine for creating humans for the world." A mad guest in the room suddenly said, "This is a descendant of Zhongnan. Perhaps he will open a Zhongnan shortcut in the realm of love. It is unknowable." Zhongnan did not argue or show any embarrassment. I know his views are genuine and cannot be judged by ordinary standards. Thus, I wrote this: "An Unconventional Couple."

Listening to Autumn Sounds at the Chrysanthemum Planting Gathering

— Jasmine

The Chrysanthemum Planting Gathering, initiated by Mr. Yu Shun'en, the owner of a Shanghai plantation, has been held at the Nanjing Road Municipal Hall for the past ten days. In addition to displaying various famous chrysanthemums, there is also a calligraphy and painting exhibition initiated by Ms. Yu Danhan and performances by various opera enthusiasts from Shanghai. On the 12th, Cheng Yanqiu performed "Qijie" as a farewell performance, causing a sensation.

When we entered, it was still 3 PM. We first went to see the calligraphy and painting, all works by modern masters. Ms. Yu Danhan has recently studied with Mr. Huang Binhong from my hometown, and her artistic skills have improved greatly. The works she displayed were elegant and extraordinary. Other works, such as Lou Xinhu's landscapes and Ma Mengrong's flowers, each had their own merits. The waterfall painting by Lou was particularly impressive in its imposing style, and viewers praised it endlessly. Mr. Li Haoran of the Xinwenbao also had calligraphy and paintings on display. Li's paintings are rarely seen by outsiders. His works are as gentle and honest as he is, truly exquisite.

While wandering around, we met several friends. I said that since the gathering is named "Chrysanthemum Planting," even if we don't have the obsession of Tao Yuanming, we should at least appreciate them a little. So we strolled around for a week together. By then, Yu Shuang had arrived, accompanied by Mr. Wang Xiaolai, who led her to the calligraphy and painting exhibition for a brief viewing. Yu Shuang is inherently elegant and praised the works of the masters. Then, some people asked Yu Shuang to sign her name as a souvenir. Immediately, dozens of people gathered around. Yu Shuang could not refuse and reluctantly obliged. As she picked up the pen, the onlookers shouted "Bravo!" After she finished signing, some shouted, "One more!" By then, she was surrounded by the crowd. It is said that she signed more than a dozen names that day.

After Yu Shuang returned to the Chrysanthemum Planting Gathering office to put on makeup, everyone knew she was about to go on stage and rushed to the hall. By then, "Ximen Bao" was coming to an end, and the audience was energized. Yu Shuang had finished her makeup and had to take the stage early. The opera "A Woman Escorted" was one that Yu Shuang had not performed since coming south this time, which made it even more anticipated. A mournful cry from behind the curtain won the full applause of the audience. Yu Shuang's costume was more beautiful than usual, and her singing was earth-shattering and universally praised, so there is no need for me to add more. However, due to the limited time that day, she only sang four lines of the "Fan Erhuang." Those who loved to hear Yu Shuang's tragic and mournful songs regretted not being able to satisfy their desire. Jiang Bogong, who played Chong Gongdao, was quite competent. However, there were too many temporarily added lines. Nevertheless, it was commendable that a new actor could handle the performance alongside a famous star so calmly. After "A Woman Escorted," there was also Wang Detian's "Caoqiao Pass." I left early because it was late, regretting not being able to hear Mr. Wang's magnificent voice.

The Great Controversy of the Small Champagne Rejection

— Xin Wei

In Shanghai, during the spring and autumn racing seasons, the purchase of champagne tickets is becoming increasingly popular. In the past, the Race Club openly sold them, but now it has gradually reached the point where non-members have no right to purchase tickets. This year, it has gone even further, only selling the numbers without issuing tickets. However, buyers are still scrambling to be the first. The A-type tickets are insufficient, so B-type tickets are added. The Chinese people's desire for luck and speculation is also growing daily. Furthermore, some groups, during the racing season, take advantage of the fact that Shanghai residents cannot buy the big champagne tickets, so they sell their so-called "small champagne" tickets. They use the winning numbers of the A-type champagne as a basis for their small champagne drawing. People from the lower and middle classes who cannot afford the big tickets switch to buying these small champagne tickets. The term "small champagne" has become a time-sensitive term in Shanghai. Some sell one number for five jiao, while others sell five to ten numbers for one yuan.

During this autumn's small champagne drawing, a controversy arose regarding a stolen ticket winning and the rejection of the prize. The Chinese and Foreign Catering Association, organized by hotel staff, serves as a recreational organization for hotel employees during their off-hours. The association, in order to raise funds, followed the example of the railway employees' club and also sold small champagne tickets. Each ticket had ten numbers and sold for one silver dollar. Tickets were sold by members. The prize money was two-thirds of the total amount, so there were many buyers.

A Russian pianist from a certain large hotel on the Bund in Nanjing Road bought a small champagne ticket from the association. Due to carelessness, he lost it on the ground. A waiter from the same hotel picked it up but did not know who had lost it at the time. The waiter sold the ticket to someone named Tao. After losing the ticket, the Russian went to the association to report the loss. The association, citing the rule that "lost tickets will not be replaced," could not reissue the ticket. The Russian could only consider himself unlucky.

Unexpectedly, when the champagne number 6 was drawn, one of the lost tickets, number 23523, from the paper with numbers from 23521 to 23530, won the second prize. Tao was overjoyed, while the Russian was devastated. The catering association did not know that the ticket was in someone's possession and mistakenly thought there was no need to pay the prize. A few days ago, Tao brought the ticket to redeem the prize, but the catering association refused to pay, saying that the ticket was the Russian's lost property and that Tao's origin was unclear. Tao swore that he had purchased it from a friend. The association firmly refused to pay. Tao argued reasonably, citing the words "no reliance on the person, no reliance on the ticket" on the ticket and explaining his source to show that he had indeed purchased it.

The association has convened a meeting of all members to discuss how to handle the matter and to investigate how the Russian's lost ticket ended up in Tao's hands. Tao has hired a lawyer to negotiate with the catering association. If they refuse to pay the prize, he will file a lawsuit to seek a legal resolution. It is said that the matter is still unresolved.

Food in Hancheng

— Tian Xian

Among Shanghai's restaurants, those of Anhui and Ningbo origins have always been the most famous. In recent years, Cantonese restaurants have also sprung up vigorously. Cantonese food is popular and gaining momentum. However, Cantonese cuisine is exquisite in general, not just in Guangzhou. Hancheng (Chaozhou) cuisine also has its own unique flavor.

In this city, only Xu Dexing's restaurant in Mantingfang is a large-scale Chaozhou restaurant. It was founded by a Chaozhou native named Xu. People from that area refer to his restaurant as "Lao Xu Zai" rather than by its store name. The dishes they prepare are extremely exquisite and palatable, not as greasy as those of Anhui and Ningbo, and fresher than Cantonese cuisine. However, because they do not advertise, customers are mostly Chaozhou people. Foreigners rarely pass by their door.

Now, the Pacific Restaurant has hired a famous chef and added Chaozhou dishes. Their cooking and presentation are far superior to Xu Dexing's. Therefore, diners all praise it. In particular, the shark fin dish is the most outstanding. Their winter seasonal specialties include raw fish hot pot, etc., which have a completely different flavor from those sold in the market. Mr. Zilan has tried it and praised its taste.

▲Short News The Paris Grand Theater has recently imported many silent feature films from abroad, which will be shown one after another. The film currently being shown is "The Soul of Beauty." This film is the most prestigious production of UFA in 1930. The lead actress is the European star Brigitte Helm. The plot is sadly glamorous, and the performance is divine and delicate. The previous hit "Scientific World" was also starred by the same actress. The next film to be shown is Ramon Novarro's "Flying World." This film is truly unprecedented in its greatness among aviation films. When this film was made, the entire fleet of the US Aviation Department performed amazing techniques. In several scenes, the planes flew over the Atlantic Ocean, hindered by violent storms and heavy rain. The engine exploded, and the plane fell into the ocean. All kinds of startling and breathtaking spectacles are truly unseen. (Ban Yun)

Travels in Southeast Asia (75)

On the morning of the 9th, Liang ordered a car to take us to see the silver mine. This is only a part of what he manages. The method is to first crush the raw ore into sand, mix it with three types of silver ore sand, and melt it in fire. If the three types are not combined, silver cannot be separated. After melting into flowing mud, it goes through several processes to become a silver ingot. It is very difficult. This mine can earn a gross income of 300,000 silver dollars per day, about 50 million per year. The capital is 20 million, and there are more than 20,000 workers. Chinese account for one-tenth, with the rest mostly being Indians. There are also Burmese. It used to have American shares, but now it is entirely British. There are only two to three hundred British people. Most of the Chinese workers are from Yunnan. Cantonese are mostly merchants or carpenters. Indians are peaceful and cannot resist others. Chinese are sometimes very fierce. The British dare not insult them either. The daily wage is at least one shield and a quarter. They only work eight hours a day. There is no holiday because the large pot needs several days to heat up once it cools down. Liang said that Chinese workers can do everything, but they cannot create delicate things because they are uneducated. However, earning foreign money here to support our people is better than being a warlord killing people and taking their wealth.

In the afternoon, I visited the Peide School. The school building is spacious and does not charge tuition. I visited the party headquarters and met with Mr. Chen Ruiwen.

There used to be eighteen Temples of the God of Wealth here, indicating great superstition. A large piece of animal skin was hanging in Liang's house. I was surprised by its size. It was very different from the ones at home. The tigers in ordinary zoos can jump ten feet high. Seeing its teeth three inches long and as thick as a thumb, it is truly a big animal. If there are no guns in the countryside and the Burmese houses are all thatched huts, it would be truly terrifying if this big animal visited. Therefore, everyone in Southeast Asia fears this mountain lord. It is not without reason. Lao Tzu said, "What everyone fears, you must fear." I also had the experience of turning pale at the mention of tigers here because I had only seen small tigers in zoos before, so I did not realize how scary they were. A friend told me how to avoid tigers: tigers are truly straightforward and do not bother chasing people to eat. They only pounce a few times. You can see how cats catch mice. If they fail to pounce three times, the tiger will give up. Therefore, the saying goes, "Tigers do not eat food they have turned away from." The way to avoid tigers is to turn around to confuse their direction, and the tiger will abandon you. Leopards, on the other hand, chase people to eat and are not as generous as the mountain lord. As for controlling snakes, once, someone was drunk and passed by a well late at night. Others warned him that there was a big snake by the well and that he should not pass by. But he insisted on passing by. The big snake was indeed there. So he lay down on the ground and looked up. The snake came and coiled around him. He struggled and rolled violently, breaking the snake's bones. As a result, the snake died. He then carried the snake back home, and everyone who saw him ran away. This is how to control snakes. Mountain people live in the mountains and understand the nature of wild animals.

European Travel Correspondence (87)

— Liu Haisu

▲Pilgrimage to Italy Diary

(3) Ten Days in Rome (9)

As we followed him into the layers of cellars, a chilling sensation suddenly touched me. Walking in a narrow, dark passage, the walls were lined with rows of niches. These niches were where the remains of the sacrificed were buried. The visible skeletons are still exposed. In this dark and eerie realm, how dark, how desolate, how cold. At this moment, I could not help but feel afraid for no reason. Suddenly, the candle in my hand went out. The cold air stabbed straight at me, as if I were being pinned down by a skeleton hidden in a niche. It seemed very close, almost touching me. After walking for a good ten minutes, it was still a dark, narrow road. A colder air was even more intense. The niches on both sides were even more intricate. They endured darkness and willingly sacrificed themselves, so they rest here forever. No, it is hard to say. Back then, they could not speak even if they wanted to. Their suffering must have been unspeakable. After passing through the narrow and dark passage, we entered a stone chamber newly discovered in the nineteenth century. Inside, there is a praiseworthy altar. It is a short hall under a dome. The dome is painted with strange flowers, lambs, peacocks, and pigeons. In the middle is a spiral staircase. As we gradually walked from the spiral staircase to the ground, it was like ascending to a bright paradise.

This is the budding of early Christian art. Later, this tradition developed and evolved into Romanesque, Byzantine, and Gothic architectural art. Finally, it produced the Renaissance. Thus, it dominated Christian culture and art for thousands of years.

Further on is the tomb of Cecilia Metella, standing on the mountain overlooking the endless oil-like green lawns, full of tall, straight palm trees. Among the trees, the intermittent aqueducts of ancient Rome stand majestically. The ancient red brick arches emit a golden-red light under the scorching sun, rendering a spicy tone, extending all the way to the distant horizon and disappearing. The dome of St. Paul's Church in the blue sky, glittering and magnificent, is truly like a brocade that can be praised. At this moment, you will forget everything and truly feel that Rome has unparalleled glory and is truly an eternal treasure trove.

After gazing at the view here, I drove back. Under a grape arbor near the Colosseum, I hurriedly ate lunch. Afterwards, we went to the embassy.

Cotton Market Sees Major Reversal

The sharp drop in cotton prices is mainly due to the fact that prices have risen for six consecutive days last week. Foreign cotton prices are weak, and the exchange rate is loose. Indian cotton combined prices are cheaper by one to two taels. However, local cotton prices have been driven up due to excessive short selling in the current month, which has led to a squeeze by buyers. As a result, forward prices have been driven up. Furthermore, the Ningbo and Shanghai groups have been aggressively purchasing in forward months, leading to a rising trend. However, Japanese and Han groups are taking advantage of this rise to sell off large quantities, totaling about 30,000 to 40,000 dan. Although futures prices have risen, spot cotton transactions in various factories remain stagnant. Japanese factories are even more inactive because they have already stocked up on cheaper Indian cotton, so they have no need to purchase more. In the afternoon, negative news about American cotton caused the market to change dramatically. The reversal was particularly severe, and many longs were fearful and sold off their positions, causing prices to trend downward across the board.

The price of Yinyuan rice fluctuated greatly, with high-quality goods priced at 13 yuan and lower-quality goods at only 10.7 or 8 jiao. With goods arriving continuously, people are taking a wait-and-see approach, and the market seems to be raising prices for the lower qualities.

Flour Market Discovering New Low Prices

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, huge price declines were seen in the market for all months. The price of foreign wheat from Chicago fell another 5 to 6 jiao, and Canadian wheat fell 1 yuan to 1.4 yuan. The price decline was even more pronounced abroad, and foreign firms were even more actively selling off their wheat. As a result, confidence was greatly impacted, and opening prices were unstable. Short sellers piled on top of each other, and sell-offs continued to be strong. The market now feels that there is a global oversupply of grain, which is sure to lead to price declines. Factories that have already ordered foreign wheat are increasing their selling volume in both the flour and wheat markets. Although long positions are trying to hold on, they are ultimately pressured by the environment. The attitude of the factories towards ordering foreign wheat is no longer based on need but entirely on speculation. As a result, new two- or three-year lows were seen across the board. This month fell 3 fen compared to the previous weekend, December fell 3 fen and a half, January fell 4 fen, and February, March, and April each fell 4 fen.

Wheat Market in a Sharp Decline

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, all months were in a sharp decline due to the impact of the sharp decline in foreign wheat prices. This month opened at 4 taels and 4 qian, followed by a large sell-off by short positions. In addition, the Zhonghua Factory was selling off wildly, regardless of the market price, which led to a collapse in the market. Long positions had little power to resist. Forward months also saw a surge in selling by factories that had already ordered foreign wheat. From the opening price to the closing price, prices also fell sharply. In the current state of affairs, if the surplus goods from abroad are imported into China in large quantities, the resulting turmoil will not only affect the flour and wheat industries. The entire society will also suffer a great loss. Those with social responsibility must pay attention to this. As a result, this month fell 1 qian and 1 fen compared to the previous weekend. December and January each fell 1 qian, and February, March, and April fell 8 fen. The spot market was very quiet because of the unfavorable environment. Wheat from Qingjiangpu, Zhongguan, opened as low as 3 taels and 6 qian, totaling more than 200 bales.

Customer Xian Rice Being Moved to Beiyang

Yesterday’s customer xian rice market saw arrivals of Jiangxi machine early and Hunan machine yuan rice. Nanjing machine rice had few in stock. Sales were lively to Beiyang group. The market was active. Prices for Nanjing rice rose by nearly a jiao. Jiangxi machine early and Hunan machine yuan were cheaper by one to two jiao due to large arrivals. Total sales for Hunan machine yuan rice were 750 bags, priced at 13 yuan 3 jiao and a half, 13 yuan 5 fen, to 12 yuan 8 jiao. Jiangxi machine early had 400 bags, priced at 10 yuan 1 jiao to 10 yuan. Nanjing machine rice had 100 bags, priced at 9 yuan 9 jiao and 9 fen. Other customer rice saw little in sales. However, if supplies increase in the future, the price of all rices may fall.

Silk and Tea Shanghai Silk Factories Reopen at 23 Factories

Silk factories in this port have been suspended due to sluggish sales and losses that were unsustainable. After persuasion by the Shanghai Silk Factory Association, silk factories in various districts have made efforts to resume operations. From the 12th to the 14th, a total of 23 silk factories in Shanghai have reopened. In the Hongkou district, Yuanfeng and nine other silk factories are currently reorganizing internally and recruiting workers. It is expected that they will be able to resume operations around the 19th. The remaining 70 silk factories have exhausted their funds and must wait for the government's silk industry bonds to be issued before they can restart production.

Needle and Eyebrow Green Tea English Sales Become Smooth

Yesterday, the tea market in this port saw sales of needle and eyebrow green tea from incoming tea estates. English firms like Jardine Matheson, Jinlong, Yuansheng, and others started to purchase, and trading was not quiet. For Gongxi green tea, Russian firms also purchased as usual. However, the selling prices were very low. The zhenmei market did not see much progress, with only medium and low-quality tea estates seeing some sales. The market price fell by one to two taels. There were still 10,000 to 20,000 boxes of Qining black tea in stock. English and Russian firms generally ignored the tea due to its poor quality. The future is bleak.

Youth Forum

Impressions of a Northern Journey

— Su Ling

(Twenty-three) Wandering Alone in Dalian City

Stepping out of the small room prepared for me by Lao Yang, what unfolded before my eyes was a streetscape displaying the filth and inferiority of the Chinese populace, a collection of complex smells, a gray, chaotic accumulation. But after I passed through this section of the city, a fresh scene spread out before me: smooth and clean roads, interesting water features, residences, small green trees... This was Seitoku Street, where the Japanese lived.

The area around the Tokiwa Bridge Chain Street is the center of metropolitan Dalian. Although there are no towering buildings, the streets with their decorative flair evoke a modern poetic sentiment.

So I passed through the quiet, shaded road again and walked into the park. Ponds, pavilions, dry trellises, broken wooden benches, shallow grass, small stone bridges... These are perfect for a Japanese girl in large sleeves and wooden sandals, leisurely, like the taste of eyes behind a shoji screen.

The other Electrical Amusement Park is also like this, with its趣味化 arrangement of small pebble paths, stone-railed bridges, small slopes, and plains of shallow grass... But this park has many animal enclosures and pools and cages for birds. There are more visitors than in the park, even though it costs five Japanese cents.

Moreover, in this park, there is a "Wooden Fish Temple," which displays all kinds of ancient and modern Chinese, Japanese, and Korean wooden fish (the percussion instrument used by monks), more than four hundred in total. Some are very large, some are extremely small. The extremely small ones are toys rather than used by monks. They are made of various woods, metals, jade, bones, shells, and artificial materials.

Leaving the Electrical Amusement Park...

In Xigang, just like Wansui Street near my residence, there are rows and rows of Chinese brothels. Each house is marked with a number. This reminds me of the brothels in Harbin and Jilin. That was extremely interesting. They were probably government-run, specially constructed as round, castle-like buildings arranged in a circle, with a pavilion in the middle and four large gates facing all directions. It's called "Circle Building." But Korean brothels write things like "Pavilion," "Building," "Cuisine," while Russian brothels have no signs. Low-class, goblin-like women stand outside the door to solicit customers.

After passing through Xigang, I took the tram back to my residence to wait for Lao Yang to return from the newspaper office so we could prepare to see Dalian at night.

Huang Jinwu's Nostalgic Tune

— Xiao Youmei

"In Memoriam" Overture to be performed by the Shanghai Municipal Orchestra at the Great Light Cinema on the evening of the 23rd of this month.

Speaking of Chinese music, it truly breaks our hearts. Kretzschmad, the president of the Berlin University of Music in Germany, said, "Even if a country has excellent musical performers, if it does not have good musical composers, it ultimately cannot be said to exist in the international music scene." When people around the world talk about music, they completely disregard China. Why is this?

Everyone who knows the slightest bit about the immensity of the world knows that musical composition is an extremely difficult task. Simply studying harmony and composition cannot be said to make one a composer. Even being able to set lyrics to music cannot be said to make one a composer. Why? Music has its own independent life. Therefore, you must break free from the limitations of words and create purely musical works. I make a firm judgment: a musician who cannot compose orchestral works, even if he creates remarkable songs, cannot be said to be a complete composer.

Because I have this understanding of musical composition, I dare not neglect the creation of orchestral works in addition to engaging in musical education. I am not trying to steal the title of composer for my own amusement, but because I believe that if a country simply does not have the creation of orchestral works, then everyone will admit that this is a national disgrace. It is truly disheartening. Although I have been very concerned about whether orchestral works have been produced in China for more than ten years, the result has always been disappointing. Unexpectedly, this time I have the opportunity to see Mr. Huang Jinwu's Nostalgic Tune. Excellent! My ten years of longing have now become a reality. Therefore, I am happy to introduce Mr. Huang Jinwu's orchestral work to all Chinese gentlemen who care about music.

The author, Mr. Huang Jinwu, told me that this is a trial work of his first orchestral piece, which is used to commemorate his girlfriend, Ms. Hu Yongfu, who has passed on to the heavens. It is also a result of Huang's study of music at Yale University in the United States. This time, he also showed me a review from a newspaper there. The newspaper featured a photo of Huang and said that Yale University usually selects the three best works from student works for the annual year-end music concert, and the one composed by that twenty-five-year-old youth—that is, Huang—was the best. This was in May 1929. Huang, who is young and energetic, achieved such valuable results in his first attempt. Isn't his future achievement limitless? Now, I will analyze the structure of Huang's Nostalgic Tune in general terms as follows:

This piece is in G minor and is divided into five major sections: (1) Introduction, (2) Opening Section, (3) Development Section, (4) Closing Section, (5) Coda. The entire piece is created from a very simple musical phrase. The simple and melancholic tune played by the cello and double bass in unison at the beginning of the introduction is the clue to the entire piece.

The opening phrase of the opening section is also an incarnation of this main musical phrase. However, in this section, it is an intense and tragic tune rather than a dull sound. The following phrase of the opening section transitions to B-flat major, which is a very soft and graceful tune. It is first played solo by the clarinet and oboe, accompanied by the extremely light and clear accompaniment of the string instruments. Later, the string instruments also join in playing the main melody and create an interesting response with the wind instruments. The closing phrase of the opening section contains some religious meaning. A simple melody is played by the wind instruments above, and the accompanying string instruments below use pizzicato to play a very clever "ground bass." Finally, the viola returns to the main musical phrase, and the tremolo on the drums adds a lot of sorrow.

The development section first elaborates on the main musical phrase, undergoing various complex changes and modulations of semitones. Suddenly, it transitions to the loudest C major. At this time, the brass instruments, like singing a triumphal song, play the following phrase of the opening section extremely magnificently. This majestic tune is as bright as the clouds parting and the sun rising. After the majestic tune, a charming tune follows, played by the flute and oboe, accompanied by the crisp arpeggios of the celesta. The musical intention of this section is also derived from the following phrase of the opening section. Then, the instruments respond to each other, gradually strengthening until the climax of the entire piece. From there, it gradually weakens and enters the fourth section.

The sections of the closing section are largely the same as the previous opening section, but are generally slightly more complex than before. For example, in the opening phrase, in addition to the celesta playing the previous main phrase, the wind instruments also create various free cyclic counterpoints based on new musical ideas. In the following phrase, what was originally a solo performance by the wind instruments has become a cyclic piece played by wind and string instruments in unison. The closing phrase also adds a section played by brass instruments, with simple chords imitating the few sections of a large organ in a church, thus intensifying the religious meaning.

The coda is still derived from the original main musical phrase, but now in C major. The previously dark and melancholic tune has suddenly turned into a bright and comforting song. The solo violin in the extremely high register makes people imagine the author's deceased friend singing sacred songs in the upper realm to comfort him, while the heavier viola plays a strict cyclic counterpoint in the lower register, a call and response between heaven and earth.

Judging from the overall structure, this is naturally a work that takes after the modelist school. Its flavor is somewhat similar to Brahms. Who doesn't know that the music of the modelist school is not the latest musical art. Originally, it is the most difficult thing to create a system of one's own. I know that Mr. Huang will not be complacent because of this. With Huang's youth and energy, and such rare musical talent, after a period of hard study, he will surely be able to create a brand-new system of his own, and win some glory for our China in the international music scene. Huang is the first person in our country to obtain a music degree from an American university music school. Because I admire Huang's talent and learning, I specially hired him as the Director of Academic Affairs and Professor of Music Theory at the National Conservatory of Music. Because his Nostalgic Tune was also praised by Mr. Pa, the conductor of the Municipal Orchestra, it was specially included in the program of the public performance on the evening of November 23 this year. This is the first time that a Chinese orchestral work has had the opportunity to be publicly performed in a Shanghai orchestra led by foreigners. Isn't this also something that all patriotic Chinese gentlemen should be most happy about?

Art Section Submission Guidelines

(1) Text is limited to news, commentary, and introductions about the latest art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature, both domestic and foreign.

(3) Photos are limited to recent portraits and works by domestic and foreign artists, and various photographs related to the text.

(4) The word count for each text should not exceed 2,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, do not write in cursive script, and use as little Western text as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not draw illustrations in the manuscript with blue ink, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black drawings must be used.

(8) Please indicate "Art Section Editorial Department" as the recipient of the submissions.

(9) Regardless of whether the submitted manuscript is published or not, it will not be returned. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance, and sufficient postage stamps should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for text is divided into three types: four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan per thousand words. Illustrations and photos are subject to the same rate per piece. Special manuscripts will be compensated separately.
